08/05/25, 9:24â€¯pm - Durvesh Chaudhari â›“ï¸: Blackouts were implemented during wartime primarily as a defensive measure to protect cities and strategic locations from aerial attacks, especially at night. Here's a breakdown of the reasons:

Reducing Visibility to Enemy Aircraft: The core reason for blackouts was to make it difficult for enemy bombers to locate and target key areas.  By eliminating or significantly reducing artificial light sources, cities became much harder to spot from the air. Â  

Targeting Difficulty: Without streetlights, illuminated landmarks, and brightly lit buildings, the visual contrast between the city and the surrounding darkness was minimized.  This made it challenging for enemy pilots to identify specific targets like factories, ports, military installations, and government buildings. Â  

Navigation Disruption: Blackouts also aimed to disrupt the navigation of enemy aircraft.  Pilots often relied on visual cues from the ground to guide them, and blackouts made it more difficult to determine their position and direction.
